    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73227612-tina-the-girl-who-lives-in-fandoms?shelf=fav-villain">fav-villain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73227612-tina-the-girl-who-lives-in-fandoms?shelf=fav-ship">fav-ship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73227612-tina-the-girl-who-lives-in-fandoms?shelf=regardless-of-age">regardless-of-age</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2278207189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4685707993793834167">before we start;<br/><b>a READERS ATTENTION!:</b><br/><br/><u>Rick Riordan's series Order:</u><br/><br/><i>first, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/40736-percy-jackson-and-the-olympians' rel='nofollow noopener'>Percy Jackson</a><br/>then <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/51379-heroes-of-olympus' rel='nofollow noopener'> Heroes of Olympus </a><br/>at last, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/162088-the-trials-of-apollo' rel='nofollow noopener'>Trials of Apollo</a> & <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/82212-magnus-chase-and-the-gods-of-asgard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Magnus Chase</a> is happening at the same time; they have crossovers sometimes.</i><br/>(or read in this order: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/183923-camp-half-blood-chronicles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Camp Half-Blood Chronicles</a>)<br/>I warned everywhere I could, because I'm nervous you might read in wrong order & you won't enjoy as much as you should.<br/><br/>anyway...<br/>generally I love the fantasy which happening in our world, low fantasy, I call them: Fantasy in reality.<br/><br/>When </span>
  <span id="freeText4685707993793834167" style="display:none">before we start;<br><b>a READERS ATTENTION!:</b><br><br><u>Rick Riordan's series Order:</u><br><br><i>first, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40736-percy-jackson-and-the-olympians" rel="nofollow noopener">Percy Jackson</a><br>then <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/51379-heroes-of-olympus" rel="nofollow noopener"> Heroes of Olympus </a><br>at last, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/162088-the-trials-of-apollo" rel="nofollow noopener">Trials of Apollo</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/82212-magnus-chase-and-the-gods-of-asgard" rel="nofollow noopener">Magnus Chase</a> is happening at the same time; they have crossovers sometimes.</i><br>(or read in this order: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/183923-camp-half-blood-chronicles" rel="nofollow noopener">Camp Half-Blood Chronicles</a>)<br>I warned everywhere I could, because I'm nervous you might read in wrong order &amp; you won't enjoy as much as you should.<br><br>anyway...<br>generally I love the fantasy which happening in our world, low fantasy, I call them: Fantasy in reality.<br><br>When fantasy elements bind in reality; we know a boring world of reality &amp; then... magic revealed! or myths, travel between universes. I live in that world &amp; I feel happy.<br>also familiar sense in other way like I know places &amp; cities (I mean in almost all high fantasy stories I'm just confused with the strange names &amp; wondering where they were.)<br>&amp; even heroes have been shocked when they actually entered their fantasy world. (so they know that world with me &amp; I can relate with their surprise, feelings, fears, etc)<br>so it made very easy to believe they can be real, somewhere, somehow, in a corner of this world magic exists (Harry Potter), you can travel to parallel universes (Pendragon) or mythology lives among us. (Percy Jackson)<br>my top fav series has another features too: they are about the subjects I actually love to know about in science. (magic, parallel universes, Myths) &amp; also they involved many awesome characters.<br><br>&amp; now whole review of one of my favourite series:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536685354i/26287435._SX540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Complete 5</b> <i>mythical</i> <b>Golden Stars</b><br><br>Idea: ★★★★★/5<br>I said thousand times that I love love love mythology, especially Greek mythology. <br>-<br>World building: ★★★★★/5<br>mythology in fantasy, sign me in!<br>I love how myths wrapped up in reality &amp; how this fiction built up. &amp; monsters, rules of this world, Demigods, villains... everything seems real &amp; realistic! I love realistic fictions. when you can just simply imagine the story is actually happening somewhere in this world. U know what I mean?😁<br>-<br>Characters: ★★★★★/5:<br>so many great characters, I mean yeah my top favourite character is Percy (&amp; Annabeth is my top fav female charcter) but there is so many great characters you simply Love &amp; can't decide which one you love more &amp; you enjoy the moments they make! characters like Tyson, Grover, Luke, Nico, Chiron, Rachel, Beckendorf, Clarisse (yeah I like her too!), Mr. D &amp; his intentional wrong names, Calypso, Bianca, Ethane, more &amp; more. I have 3 favourite gods (Apollo, Poseidon, Hades)<br><br>I always say:<br><i>Great characters make a great story, great!</i><br>(&amp; great idea &amp; written style &amp; humor of course, but first I should find a character I care about.(here, in this series, are more than just one; also like in other Rick Riordan's series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2214868217" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2349940498" rel="nofollow noopener">Pendragon</a> &amp; some more))<br><br>&amp; their developments are very realistic &amp; fantastic!<br><br>those parts when they are brave &amp; inspire you to be brave in your life.<br>the "I can do it" power<br><br>&amp; my top OTP is here!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536677564i/26286838._SY540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536677564i/26286839._SY540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>-<br>Written style: ★★★★★/5<br>even though it's 1st person, I love it &amp; how Percy describes what he is dealing with.<br>/HUMOR!: ★★★★★/5<br>&amp; the laughter is infinite!<br>/feelz: ★★★★★/5 <br>happy &amp; sad emotions are essential for every great stories. I love to have tears of Joy, or my heart wrenches during reading a book &amp; Riordan knows how to make us cry, even over a not-important character we don't care about.<br>-<br>plot: ★★★★★/5<br>Every pages my heart is racing. every events are adrenaline rush, &amp; I love to feel the excitements!<br>&amp; Riordan knows how to put a Plot twist! thrilling!<br>➖➖➖➖<br>&lt; my reviews &gt;: Golden Stars<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2169282743" rel="nofollow noopener">the Lightning Thief</a> : ★★★★(★)/5<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2169299870" rel="nofollow noopener">the Sea of Monsters</a> : ★★★★(★)/5<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2169285403" rel="nofollow noopener">the Titan's Curse</a>: ★★★★★/5<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2169299949" rel="nofollow noopener">the Battle of Labyrinth</a>: ★★★★★/5<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2169300053" rel="nofollow noopener">the Last Olympian</a> : ★★★★★/5<br><br>&amp; did anyone notice that each book has a kind of reference retelling of a special Greek Hero? (I didn't either, I read somewhere &amp; this just blown my mind! Riordan is a genius!)<br>-<br>𝒯𝒽𝒶𝓃𝓀𝓈 𝒻𝑜𝓇 𝓈𝓉𝑜𝓅𝓅𝒾𝓃𝑔 𝒷𝓎!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12571188980488241602">I am as obsessed as a person can be with PJ. Annabeth is so cool, Grover is so hilarious and Percy (at least in the movie) is SUCH a hottie! I watched the movie only hours ago and yes, it's true: they practically ripped the book apart. Where's Clarisse? That's what I ask. Where's Dionysus and Annabeth's dream of being an architect and relationship with Luke and Grover's obsession with Pan and the REAL way Percy came across the pearls? They were never Persephone's. I mean, Grover is white! Annabe</span>
  <span id="freeText12571188980488241602" style="display:none">I am as obsessed as a person can be with PJ. Annabeth is so cool, Grover is so hilarious and Percy (at least in the movie) is SUCH a hottie! I watched the movie only hours ago and yes, it's true: they practically ripped the book apart. Where's Clarisse? That's what I ask. Where's Dionysus and Annabeth's dream of being an architect and relationship with Luke and Grover's obsession with Pan and the REAL way Percy came across the pearls? They were never Persephone's. I mean, Grover is white! Annabeth is blond with piercing gray eyes! You have no idea the disappointment I feel when someone tells me they've seen the movie but haven't read the book. You haven't experienced Percy's story UNTIL you've read the book. SO, let's chalk this one up. BOOK: 10 million points. MOVIE: Goose egg.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1293178865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer232204780110661672">Doing the review this way, rather than writing one for each book :)<br/>----<br/><br/>This series is right up there with Harry Potter and Henning Mankell's Kurt Wallander series as my top favorite series. Each re-visit is dropping in on some old friends and re-living their adventures/lives.<br/><br/>First time I saw this series, I was passing the book section at work and the movie cover caught my eye (I think the movie was out not long after I finished the book). The title and synopsis immediately intrigued me and on a </span>
  <span id="freeText232204780110661672" style="display:none">Doing the review this way, rather than writing one for each book :)<br />----<br /><br />This series is right up there with Harry Potter and Henning Mankell's Kurt Wallander series as my top favorite series. Each re-visit is dropping in on some old friends and re-living their adventures/lives.<br /><br />First time I saw this series, I was passing the book section at work and the movie cover caught my eye (I think the movie was out not long after I finished the book). The title and synopsis immediately intrigued me and on a whim I bought it on my next break.<br /><br />So started the love affair :) <br /><br />I loved Mr. Riordan's take on the half bloods and monsters, Percy was easy to root for (although sometimes you did want to smack him) and Annabeth/Grover/Nico/Tyson quickly became my favorites among the campers.<br />The Gods... haha, well... a love/hate relationship there. The banter between them was great but sometimes they reminded me of kids throwing a temper tantrum. Poseidon and Artemis were my top favorites (I probably would have joined the Hunters). <br /><br />Ares reminded me of a bully at times but not a bad ally to have on your side I suppose...<br /><br />Does series really need more reviews? Probably not :) I'm throwing my two cents in anyway :-P<br /><br />I would recommend this for all ages, just a fun series with great characters and plenty of humor/drama thrown in to balance the other stuff out (a certain scene in the 5th book with a certain someone getting squashed by a certain something in battle always cracks me up). <br /><br />The audiobook narrator Jesse Bernstein does a marvelous job bringing everyone/everything to life. He does all five books, which is great and I never had problems telling who was who when he was doing his thing... so check them out if you can :)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="232204780110661672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1638596254534777732">This set was recommended to me by a 9th grader, and I'm giving the hardcover set to my granddaughter on her 10th birthday. While the writing style is not up to my J.K.Rowling yardstick, the books offer good characters and an unusual premise. Percy and others are "demigods", meaning that one of their parents is a Greek god. Thus, Riordan also brings young readers into the world of mythology while providing an entertaining action storyline.<br/><br/><br/>As with the Potter books, one of my favorite characteristi</span>
  <span id="freeText1638596254534777732" style="display:none">This set was recommended to me by a 9th grader, and I'm giving the hardcover set to my granddaughter on her 10th birthday. While the writing style is not up to my J.K.Rowling yardstick, the books offer good characters and an unusual premise. Percy and others are "demigods", meaning that one of their parents is a Greek god. Thus, Riordan also brings young readers into the world of mythology while providing an entertaining action storyline.<br /><br /><br />As with the Potter books, one of my favorite characteristics if that the books focus on friendship rather than moving into any type of romance. In book one, THE LIGHTNING THIEF, Percy (short for Perseus) is 11, and becomes a year older in each book.<br /><br />The set of 5 is rather uneven, with the third book, THE TITAN'S CURSE, being my favorite. Riordan may not have Rowling's great descriptive style, but he HAS provided a good storyline and some memorable characters.</span>

<div id="review_214145308" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/214145308" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4670084-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405261416p2/4670084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/214145308?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/4670084-katie">Katie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4670084-katie?shelf=5-star-books">5-star-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer214145308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6666277622834494200">So many reviews of this series compare it to Harry Potter (and with good reason) but as a fan of both (and a beginning skeptic myself) I have to say that though they are similar series, Percy Jackson stands on its own. In the Lightening Thief, Percy is so Harry Potter, the camp is so Hogwarts, Chiron is so Dumbledore- I completely admit that. In fact when this series first came out I refused to read it and criticized it for being a rip-off. But for some reason, I gave it a try (at the request of</span>
  <span id="freeText6666277622834494200" style="display:none">So many reviews of this series compare it to Harry Potter (and with good reason) but as a fan of both (and a beginning skeptic myself) I have to say that though they are similar series, Percy Jackson stands on its own. In the Lightening Thief, Percy is so Harry Potter, the camp is so Hogwarts, Chiron is so Dumbledore- I completely admit that. In fact when this series first came out I refused to read it and criticized it for being a rip-off. But for some reason, I gave it a try (at the request of a friend) and really loved it. The further along the series goes, the farther away Percy Jackson is from Harry Potter. Percy's voice is the reason to read YA- it's clever and sweet, witty and touching. I think Riordan's greatest achievement in this series is the characters- especially Percy. You really begin to feel for him and you believe he is completely capable and brave but it's not overboard- he is not an adult-version of a 15 year old. <br /><br />For me, the similarities between the two series boils down to generic similarities over the course of Percy Jackson. An extraordinary boy who never understood why he was so unaccepted and or different in his world, until it is relieved to him that he is powerful beyond belief (in some way or another). From here, he enters into a world where he is not only accepted by revered and has the weight of the world upon his shoulders. To accomplish a challenging and, in some ways hopeless, role he is helped by his loyal friends. That is Harry Potter. That is Percy Jackson. That is Ender Wiggin. Tweak it a little and that could be Jonah from the Giver or Thomas from The Maze Runner or really any YA dystopian for that matter. <br /><br />My point is, if you are a fan of end-of-the-world, fantasy, powerful children, and YA, then you will really enjoy the Percy Jackson and the Olympians series. Don't brush it aside because of similarities to Harry Potter, enjoy it for it's own creative, witty world which is a true pleasure to explore. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6666277622834494200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1492486315" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1492486315" />
    <a title="Irina Elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7664770-irina-elena"><img alt="Irina Elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587303756p2/7664770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1492486315?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irina Elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irina Elena" href="/user/show/7664770-irina-elena">Irina Elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18813911-percy-jackson">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=paranormal-or-urban-fantasy">paranormal-or-urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=ya-pnr">ya-pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1492486315" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11068122678301356022">Don't mind me, just getting used to sharing my thoughts with the world again.<br/>Here goes.<br/><br/>This was pretty fucking awesome. Unexpectedly so, to be honest.<br/>I never even considered reading this series until I saw the two movies back to back on TV on a random night, and I got so into them I just <i>had</i> to read the series. (You know you've written a lot of reviews when the GR html code comes naturally to your fingers even after an almost year-long hiatus. Huh.) Thank god I decided to start from the first bo</span>
  <span id="freeText11068122678301356022" style="display:none">Don't mind me, just getting used to sharing my thoughts with the world again.<br />Here goes.<br /><br />This was pretty fucking awesome. Unexpectedly so, to be honest.<br />I never even considered reading this series until I saw the two movies back to back on TV on a random night, and I got so into them I just <i>had</i> to read the series. (You know you've written a lot of reviews when the GR html code comes naturally to your fingers even after an almost year-long hiatus. Huh.) Thank god I decided to start from the first book, because the movie producers basically ripped the whole thing to shreds and then used them to make something completely different – which is not necessarily a bad thing, since there would've been no way to fit the entire plot of <i>The Lightning Thief</i> in a 90 minute movie, but don't expect to be able to follow the actual series if you start from book 3.<br /><br />That being said, I have two main points to make.<br />1. This is nothing like HP, and I don't know what people are smoking.<br />Sure, there are three friends going on dangerous fantastical adventures and saving the people they love slash the world. And yes, there are also lessons to be learned from these adventures. But that's where the similarities end.<br />The characters' personalities and backgrounds are completely different, the author's tone is much more dynamic, boyish and sarcastic, and the atmosphere is far from Hogwartsy. Do not go into this expecting to find what you've been missing since HP ended, because you won't. And this ties into my second point, which is:<br />2. <i>Do</i> go into this expecting considerable amounts of fun and excitement and something wildly refreshing. Okay, that last one mostly applies to me, I think, because I tend to shy away from both MG novels and works inspired by classical mythology because of mostly unfunded prejudices (get your shit together, Nina, good lord). So to me, this type of story was fairly new, and honestly felt like a breath of fresh air. All the adventure, and the fighting, and the monsters, and the life-or-death situations? I dig. <i>A lot.</i><br /><br />It's just <i>good</i>, guys. Genuinely, shockingly good, and gripping and funny and sad and all that awesome stuff. There is actual character growth, not a boring moment, and continuous surprises. What's not to love?<br />Okay, yeah, I had a few nits to pick, because otherwise I wouldn't be me, so it doesn't get a full five stars. But I read the whole thing in a week, and my final verdict is completely, overwhelmingly positive. On to <i>Heroes of Olympus</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11068122678301356022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2149326342" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sinead" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sinead" href="/user/show/13986510-sinead">Sinead</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2149326342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8965094063132236280">I really wish I’d read this series when I was around twelve and feel a nostalgic connection towards it. Because if I can love it even at twenty three, I know I would’ve just adored it for the intended age. The same with Harry Potter. <br/><br/>However, I’m still so glad I read it now. I always hear so many amazing things about this series so I am so happy I get to join in on the fandom! <br/><br/>This series is so fantastical and great, and Percy’s voice is such a fantastic one to experience. He grows so much over </span>
  <span id="freeText8965094063132236280" style="display:none">I really wish I’d read this series when I was around twelve and feel a nostalgic connection towards it. Because if I can love it even at twenty three, I know I would’ve just adored it for the intended age. The same with Harry Potter. <br /><br />However, I’m still so glad I read it now. I always hear so many amazing things about this series so I am so happy I get to join in on the fandom! <br /><br />This series is so fantastical and great, and Percy’s voice is such a fantastic one to experience. He grows so much over the course of the 5 books – he grows from an insecure 12 year old boy unsure of who he is and weary over this new world he’s entered to a confident young man capable of taking down a Titan. I was so proud of him by the end!<br /><br />Rick Riordan has such an amazing imagination, and he brought the world of half-bloods and monsters to life with such ease, and it’s so easy to imagine that there really is a world of demi-gods out there which we don’t see because of the Mist. You fall in love with every character, and all we want is for our heroes to prevail.<br /><br />I loved seeing Percy interact with his father Poseidon, and his bond with the other campers and his half-brother. <br /><br />Annabeth and Percy were just great, friends naturally turned into romantic interests, (even though I wish it hadn’t happened at the VERY end of the series, it would’ve been nice to see them as boyfriend/girlfriend for more than a few paragraphs). But here’s hoping they turn up in the spinoff books!<br /><br />I know this series probably doesn’t need any more reviews but here are my thoughts anyway. If there’s anybody not sure whether to pick up this book series or not, I say go for it. It’s a world you enter which you never truly leave. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8965094063132236280" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_663806153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/663806153" />
    <a title="Alienor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16589170-alienor"><img alt="Alienor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530109097p2/16589170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/663806153?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor" href="/user/show/16589170-alienor">Alienor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer663806153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18434721523932713727">Ok, so the Percy Jackson series is *readable. And yes, it gives an 'easy' way into Greek mythology to teenagers - although why teenagers can't read the actual thing since it is a rollicking great ball of fun, I don't understand.<br/>But, hm. It's a bit glib. It is chockful of American private jokes, Dead'R Us and the like, which will not be funny to non-Americans. It also doesn't quite gel. If Percy knows he's going to have to fight monsters daily now and forever, why does he insist on going back to </span>
  <span id="freeText18434721523932713727" style="display:none">Ok, so the Percy Jackson series is *readable. And yes, it gives an 'easy' way into Greek mythology to teenagers - although why teenagers can't read the actual thing since it is a rollicking great ball of fun, I don't understand.<br />But, hm. It's a bit glib. It is chockful of American private jokes, Dead'R Us and the like, which will not be funny to non-Americans. It also doesn't quite gel. If Percy knows he's going to have to fight monsters daily now and forever, why does he insist on going back to normal mortal schools (high school!) where he learns nothing because of his ADHD and from which he gets expelled each year anyway? Why, while he could be going to 'Camp Half-Blood' (don't like the name...) and practice fighting, thus, I don't know, saving his life!?<br />Grover is the perfect sidekick, not too smart, not too brave - and feels like 'the Black token', especially in the movies.<br />The gods expect their kids - whom they never even see! some kids don't know who their godly parent is! - to fight their own battles while they do nothing until the last book. Percy firmly enjoins a few characters to support their godly parent 'because he's your dad/mom'. <br />Hum, so what? What does one owe a parent one has never met?<br />Gods and mythical creatures are tossed around without a clear sense of coherence. Alliances are not built up, things keep popping up with the self-named 'heroes' running after them.<br />Also, I felt that when the story was in a tight corner, Rick Riordan would pull JKRowling-like themes out of his hat. Oh, of course, sacrifice, the death of a parent (faked in this case), the trio of friends, giant half-brothers, a school with 'houses' and a wise counselor, an evil guy who is very like the hero, the use of hidden and convenient prophecies, the use of magical artifacts that look mundane in the mortal world, the threat on the same mortals (but only in America)...etc do not belong exclusively to Rowling - but what can I say, she does it better. She creates a build-up with character growth, while Rick Riordan seems a little halfhazard in his choices.<br />Honestly, read the real thing, ie Mythology. It IS so deeply woven into our culture it will echo within anyone, and it's FUN and rich and beautiful and absolutely not moralizing. Percy Jackson just tastes like icing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18434721523932713727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3340428655" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Will Ansbacher" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5072847-will-ansbacher"><img alt="Will Ansbacher" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485713675p2/5072847.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3340428655?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will Ansbacher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will Ansbacher" href="/user/show/5072847-will-ansbacher">Will Ansbacher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3340428655" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17277766085891740923">I read the five volumes of <i>PJ and the Olympians</i> to my 9 year old granddaughter. She absolutely loved them all, so this rating is an average of her 5++++ and my 3+ ish stars. <br/><br/>I thought the first volume <i> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28187.The_Lightning_Thief__Percy_Jackson_and_the_Olympians___1_' title='The Lightning Thief (Percy Jackson and the Olympians, #1) by Rick Riordan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lightning Thief</a></i> was pretty good, excellent even, weaving the mythology of the Greek gods into the tale of Percy (short for Perseus), an 11-year old in New York with an attention disorder, who also happens to be a demi-god, the son of Poseidon and a mortal NY mother. He faces a dangerous missio</span>
  <span id="freeText17277766085891740923" style="display:none">I read the five volumes of <i>PJ and the Olympians</i> to my 9 year old granddaughter. She absolutely loved them all, so this rating is an average of her 5++++ and my 3+ ish stars. <br /><br />I thought the first volume <i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28187.The_Lightning_Thief__Percy_Jackson_and_the_Olympians___1_" title="The Lightning Thief (Percy Jackson and the Olympians, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lightning Thief</a></i> was pretty good, excellent even, weaving the mythology of the Greek gods into the tale of Percy (short for Perseus), an 11-year old in New York with an attention disorder, who also happens to be a demi-god, the son of Poseidon and a mortal NY mother. He faces a dangerous mission, where the fate of the world appears to be in his hands, and it’s to be completed before he turns 16. The action is fast-paced although a bit repetitive for an adult reader, as Percy battles cleverly-arranged encounters with just about all the major gods, whose personalities are true to their Greek origins (I loved that they were enraged to be called “mythological” rather than actual 3000-year old beings) - and some minor gods (who are engagingly grumpy about their lesser status). Percy is aided by a motley band of other demigod outcasts, centaurs, cyclopes and so on.<br />In short - very imaginative, loaded with snappy dialogue, and touching on a number of social issues from bullying to step-parents without being at all preachy. I even learned a bit of Greek mythology!<br /><br />But as I read the rest of the series (one after another, without a break!), I became increasingly impatient. Not so much because the battle themes were repetitive (they were), but as Percy aged towards 16, one volume per year, the female characters in particular became harder to take. Every one of them, even the goddesses, started to act the drama queen, just as Percy became more and more the upstanding resolute hero. OK, I know Riordan is trying to catch the interest of North American teens here, but this is <i>fantasy</i>, and in pandering to his target market’s stereotypes, he really missed an opportunity for some role modelling. <br /><br />I also felt Riordan’s location-naming became increasingly obsessive, reaching a fever pitch of precision in the final volume <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4502507.The_Last_Olympian__Percy_Jackson_and_the_Olympians___5_" title="The Last Olympian (Percy Jackson and the Olympians, #5) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Olympian</a>
</i> where the battle for Mt Olympus (a <i>fantasy</i> structure, I should note, hovering above the Empire State Building) is catalogued intersection by friggin' intersection! <br />To preserve my sanity (and where Ms. eagle-eyes wasn’t reading along) I omitted the exact route from the Williamsburg Bridge to downtown Manhattan, the giant pig’s taking a flying right “at East 42nd St to 5th Avenue” and many more. Did Riordan write this with a Lonely Planet guide open? Sheesh!<br />(Also, I was a little disappointed that he hadn’t made use of the USA’s actual Mt. Olympus, which I can almost see from the end of my street. That would have been cool, but maybe it wasn’t in his travel guide.) <br /><br />OK, by the end my discreet eye-rolling phase was over, the narrative had redeemed itself somewhat, the ending was surprising and a pretty good one at that - and the drama from the females was much abated, so I guess I would recommend it!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17277766085891740923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_71963039" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71963039" />
    <a title="Molly G" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/751010-molly-g"><img alt="Molly G" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1230148327p2/751010.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71963039?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Molly G" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Molly G" href="/user/show/751010-molly-g">Molly G</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/751010-molly-g?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/751010-molly-g?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/751010-molly-g?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/751010-molly-g?shelf=adfi">adfi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71963039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4752738684652930018">Favorite: book IV - <i>Battle of the Labyrinth</i><br/><br/>I majored in Greek mythology at college, so I can say happily, with some authority, that Riordan really knows his stuff and gets it right. No matter how brief the reference and how it's reused for the adventure, he gives snippets that kids, anyone, can latch onto and be consistent with more academic approaches. Also means, if you're already familiar with the mythology, he lets you feel very clever by letting you recognize a being a page in advance befor</span>
  <span id="freeText4752738684652930018" style="display:none">Favorite: book IV - <i>Battle of the Labyrinth</i><br /><br />I majored in Greek mythology at college, so I can say happily, with some authority, that Riordan really knows his stuff and gets it right. No matter how brief the reference and how it's reused for the adventure, he gives snippets that kids, anyone, can latch onto and be consistent with more academic approaches. Also means, if you're already familiar with the mythology, he lets you feel very clever by letting you recognize a being a page in advance before he reveals who/what they are. (Catch the uncommented-upon <i>Iliad</i> homage sequence in Book V.) I like the idea of someone reading this as a child, going on to study the mythology more formally later on, and recognizing many of the elements and enjoying how the fictional use melds with the originals — and probably finding it all easier to follow and remember for that.<br /><br />Of course, I can't help comparing to <i>Harry Potter</i> (though that's kind of silly, since kids-discovering-they're-really-some-kind-of-supernatural-being is a genre that existed long before). That's okay, <i>PJ</i> doesn't suffer by the comparison. Like Rowling, Riordan is excellent writing engaging adventures that are fast, enjoyable reads; and have plots that build consistently and elaborately to surprising reveals, within each book and across the series. A few contrasts that I really appreciate in <i>PJ:</i> I like the world continuity of using a single mythology (very well!), and the bringing of mythical Greek elements to present-day NYC are very clever, from cultural and humorous standpoints as well as educational. I also enjoy how the plot, without betraying any of the information that's established and developed through the book, usually ends up to be about something quite unexpected and different from the conclusions the characters and reader were drawing all along. Likewise, there's more room for characters to move outside expectations, sympathies, and archetypes, but never randomly or in betrayal of how they've been established.<br /><br />A fun, fast read, which contains well-considered factoids you won't even realize you're picking up.<br /><br /><br /><br />8/15/13: reread "Lightning Thief". As much as I enjoyed it the first time, seems even *better* compared to the movies. ;-) Seriously, as ever: very intelligent and awesome, and really knowns its mythology. Plots within plots, moral ambiguity/politicking, and thoroughly touching loyalties.<br /><br />8/16/13: reread "Sea of Monsters". Book wonderful, doesn't deserve it but review will be overshadowed by having just seen the movie. I never understand the Lynch-Dune Syndrome: omitting awesome, cinematic action sequences from the book to be replaced with lamer made-up action sequences in the movie. Doesn't make it more exciting or anything... just dumbed down. Rereading the book, among other things, was a sequence of: "Ohhhhh yeah, <i>that's</i> why that bit makes sense…" One of the odder (and to me, more angering) things the movie did was keeping Grover in the wedding dress to fool Polyphemus, but have P. think G. was a "housemaid" rather than prospective wife. Seriously? That's along the lines of "PATROCLUS WAS NOT ACHILLES'S <i>COUSIN,</i> 'TROY'!!" …Although I do appreciate that Annabeth took the Odysseus role, from the Sirens to the Nobody ploy. Very cool.<br /><br />8/17/13: reread "Titan's Curse". Bought it in the morning, read most of it on the beach, finished it in the bath. Which, all in all, is very appropriate. Another great installment—I can't tell if they get better as the series progresses, or it's just the awesome buildup of layers and complexities. Which may be the same thing, but is not a difference in the writing quality, just in having installments. There are bits of this that stuck with me more clearly from the first reading than almost anything in the previous books; the Di Angelos are so memorable, as is the unwritten prequel of the exploits of Thalia, Luke and Annabeth. And Artemis ROCKS. As does Apollo. As ever, love Riordan's really great depth of knowledge with the mythology and intensely faithful and clever ways he plays with it. And, something that's become a bigger issue for me since my first reading, these books kick almost everything else's ass in terms of passing the Bechdel Test and beyond. Name another series where in any given scene the female protagonists outnumber the male. As well as not only being cool but being <i>different</i> from each other. Thank you, Riordan; really awesome. May still be a male titular narrator, but still kicking almost everyone else's butt on the female-role-model-representation front.<br /><br />8/20/13: reread "Battle of the Labyrinth". Don't know if it's still my favorite, but another cracker nonetheless! Guess they're all fitting together pretty seamlessly now so one doesn't stand out so much from the whole. I like the device of different focal gods per book; really helps set each individual tone. And as I've always said since first reading: DAMN is Riordan good with the source material (mythology). I think I will read Kane Chronicles for upcoming plane trip: I trust him on the Greek and Roman mythology I know a lot about, so I'm prepared to trust him on the Egyptian mythology I know very little about. Might be interesting to test my theory of "people who read this not knowing much about the mythology may pick it up".<br /><br />8/22/13: reread "The Last Olympian". Happiness! Oh, I do love this one. So much I'd forgotten and what a joy to be reminded. I love the "Iliad" references so much—all the moreso for going entirely uncommented on in the narrative. I love the definitions/distribution of "heroism" (as theme, action, and characteristic). I love how the identity/nature of the "Last Olympian" fits into my undergraduate Classics thesis, for pete's sake. ("Homecoming" as the final requisite Epic Element.) The only downside is that I'm done with the series now. Alas. I suppose I could give one of Riordan's other serii a go…</span>
  <a data-text-id="4752738684652930018" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Characters could have been developed further but I guess it would probably satisfy its young audience. <div id="review_3606394266" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3606394266" />
    <a title="Payel Rana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/115663213-payel-rana"><img alt="Payel Rana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596517130p2/115663213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

  <span id="freeText16545761775981947385" style="display:none">The best part about the series is the intermingling of myth,legend and fresh fiction, woven around new characters.<br />You dive into a world of gods,monsters,heroes and mortals with beautiful portrayl of friendship, courage, trust, acceptance of flaws and bravery.<br /><br />Now about it being compared to Harry Potter: The milieu are beautiful, bewitching and play on subtle humor BUT the characters don't grow on you much (probably coz none of the major ones die!) and since the series is extended into further books, you're left hungry for more. There's a finale but not the end.<br /><br />P.S.: Do read "The Demigod Files" in between the 4th and 5th book.</span>

<div id="review_1153541215" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1153541215" />
    <a title="Joya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33606325-joya"><img alt="Joya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478491974p2/33606325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1153541215?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joya" href="/user/show/33606325-joya">Joya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1153541215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10002760869125021768"><b>
  <i>
    <u>The Books:</u>
  </i>
</b><br/>The Lightning Thief<br/>The Sea of Monsters<br/>The Titan's Curse<br/>The Battle of the Labyrinth<br/>The Last Olympian<br/><br/><b>
  <u>
    <i>The Characters:</i>
  </u>
</b><br/><br/><b>Perseus 'Percy' Jackson-</b>By far probably my favorite male fictional character and one of my overall favorite fictional characters of all time. Percy is such a sarcastic character and can be a bit clueless sometimes, but is still very smart and just an overall amazing character. He is also extremely loyal and was very well developed.<br/><br/><b>Annabeth Chase-</b>Like</span>
  <span id="freeText10002760869125021768" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <u>The Books:</u>
  </i>
</b><br />The Lightning Thief<br />The Sea of Monsters<br />The Titan's Curse<br />The Battle of the Labyrinth<br />The Last Olympian<br /><br /><b>
  <u>
    <i>The Characters:</i>
  </u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Perseus 'Percy' Jackson-</b>By far probably my favorite male fictional character and one of my overall favorite fictional characters of all time. Percy is such a sarcastic character and can be a bit clueless sometimes, but is still very smart and just an overall amazing character. He is also extremely loyal and was very well developed.<br /><br /><b>Annabeth Chase-</b>Like Percy, Annabeth is my favorite fictional character out of the females though and is actually probably my favorite character of all time. Like Hermione Granger from J.K. Rowling's Harry Potter, Annabeth shows that just because you are a girl and know a lot of things, it doesn;t mean that you can't kick butt.<br /><br /><b>Grover Underwood-</b>Grover is an amazing character. I love how his character was developed through the series. He is still pretty klutzy a lot of the time, but if he wasn't he wouldn't be Grover. He may be a scaredy-cat or well scaredy-goat, but he is still really brave if you ask me.<br /><br /><b>Luke Castellan-</b> There isn't much I can say about Luke without spoiling things, but then again that's kind of this whole review. Although Luke made some bad choices, he made up for them in the end.<br /><br /><b>Thalia Grace-</b>I've always loved Thalia. She kind of reminded me of myself in a way that is kind of hard to put into words, although Annabeth reminds me of myself much more. Thalia is such a strong and amazing character and I wish we got to see more of her.<br /><br /><b>Nico di Angelo-</b> Oh my gods, Nico. I really love Nico. One of my favorite characters of all time and probably ties with Percy for my favorite male character. He had to go through so much at such a young age.<br /><br /><b>Tyson-</b> This little guy came into our lives during <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28186.The_Sea_of_Monsters__Percy_Jackson_and_the_Olympians___2_" title="The Sea of Monsters (Percy Jackson and the Olympians, #2) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sea of Monsters</a>, although I guess you can't really call him little, can you?<br /><br /><b>Zeus-</b>Not to be disrespectful to Lord Zeus of anything, but if you actually look back at everything in the Greek Myths, if something bad happened is probably because Zeus thought that his position as King of Olympus was threatened or he just couldn't keep it in his pants.<br /><br /><b>Chiron-</b>Chiron was a great teacher for many great heroes and I am pretty sure that he became a father figure to many <i>many</i> heroes.<br /><br /><b>Dionysus-</b>I actually find how Rick pictured him to be quite funny, although I am pretty sure that it would be true. I'm pretty sure that he doesn't try to get heroes' names rights so that he doesn't get attached to them, but it's just a thought.<br /><br /><b>Ares-</b>Is an arrogant upstart, that's all I have to say.<br /><br /><b>Poseidon-</b> I love the idea of him always wearing a Hawaiian shirt and Bermuda shorts and find it oddly amusing.<br /><br /><b>Clarisse La Rue-</b>An Amazing character, I love her.<br /><br /><b>Sally Jackson-</b>An amazing mother and woman. She is such a strong person.<br /><br /><b>Paul Blofis-</b>I'm glad that he is now with Sally. He is actually really cool, to be honest.<br /><br /><b>Hermes-</b>I really like George and Martha. Hermes is really funny and is actually one of my favorite deities in the Greek Myths.<br /><br /><b>Apollo-</b>Enough with the haikus Apollo. I can't wait to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26252859.The_Hidden_Oracle__The_Trials_of_Apollo___1_" title="The Hidden Oracle (The Trials of Apollo, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hidden Oracle</a> to get more of Apollo's weird personality.<br /><br /><b>Artemis-</b>Probably my favorite goddess.<br /><br /><b>Athena-</b>Tied with Artemis for my favorite goddess, although she can be kind of...rude.<br /><br /><b>Hera-</b>I hate her and her stupid cows.<br /><br /><b>Hades-</b>By far my favorite god, and beats everyone for my favorite. He is awesome.<br /><br /><b>Hestia-</b>She is too kind for her own good.<br /><br /><b>Other Characters-</b>Ethan was pretty cool. I was pretty sad about Zoe, Bianca, Silena, and Beckendorf. Blackjack was just awesome. I just love Rick's Characters.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>
    <i>Synopsis:</i>
  </u>
</b><br /><br /><b>The Plot-</b>Was great and was able to keep the story exciting and kept the story moving.<br /><br /><b>The Ending-</b>Great, fantastic, amazing, for each book.<br /><br /><b>What I Love-</b>Everything.<br /><br /><b>What I Didn't Love-</b>Nothing, I loved everything.<br /><br /><b>Final Thoughts-</b> Each book was amazing, and I loved rereading them all. Percy Jackson is still my favorite series ever.<br /><br /><b>Final Rating-</b>The average rating is 5/5 stars. And it was definitly deserved.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10002760869125021768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Anchit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7153124-anchit"><img alt="Anchit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474339620p2/7153124.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/536665852?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anchit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anchit" href="/user/show/7153124-anchit">Anchit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer536665852" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3361196664339776759">I found it too kiddish - maybe it's because I'm almost 30. Don't get me wrong. Ive read the harry potter series and loved them so much that I saw all their movies and played their pc games too. But this one is too predictable on a lot of occasions:<br/><br/>1) bad guy comes, irritates/tortures hero, hero does a strike move, wins, praise, cheesy dialogues and lots of "how did i do that". it gets boring pretty fast.<br/><br/>2) hero asks qs, answered with riddles, more qs more riddles, someone else comes into the pic</span>
  <span id="freeText3361196664339776759" style="display:none">I found it too kiddish - maybe it's because I'm almost 30. Don't get me wrong. Ive read the harry potter series and loved them so much that I saw all their movies and played their pc games too. But this one is too predictable on a lot of occasions:<br /><br />1) bad guy comes, irritates/tortures hero, hero does a strike move, wins, praise, cheesy dialogues and lots of "how did i do that". it gets boring pretty fast.<br /><br />2) hero asks qs, answered with riddles, more qs more riddles, someone else comes into the picture who is very reputed and the conversation stops. this someone else regards hero lower than himself but just then or maybe sometime later event (1 above) happens. Now this guy holds the hero in very high regard and explains some stuff to him.<br /><br />3) hero is just doing his normal daily stuff. Someone comes up to him and either starts taunting him or starts chatting with him. Either way the hero is told some amazing facts and now he goes to character (2 above) and gets a lot of explanation about it.<br /><br />The same cycle keeps repeating endlessly. so i stopped halfway through the book. too bad i wont read the rest of the series.</span>

<div id="review_871653847" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/871653847" />
    <a title="Isabelle Jade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29185783-isabelle-jade"><img alt="Isabelle Jade" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502391365p2/29185783.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/871653847?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isabelle Jade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isabelle Jade" href="/user/show/29185783-isabelle-jade">Isabelle Jade</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29185783-isabelle-jade?shelf=middle-reader">middle-reader</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29185783-isabelle-jade?shelf=favorite-female-characters">favorite-female-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer871653847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13536935194375762442">I don't actually have/never read this particular boxed set edition, but it was the only one I could find that included all the books. I read the Percy Jackson series quite a while ago, and then again last year, and both readings were enjoyable. I was a bit skeptical of the writing (I was not sure that I would like the first person narration of a teen aged boy) but was surprised that it caught me. I love the Mythology theme, and the characters, and I never was bored during any of the books. They </span>
  <span id="freeText13536935194375762442" style="display:none">I don't actually have/never read this particular boxed set edition, but it was the only one I could find that included all the books. I read the Percy Jackson series quite a while ago, and then again last year, and both readings were enjoyable. I was a bit skeptical of the writing (I was not sure that I would like the first person narration of a teen aged boy) but was surprised that it caught me. I love the Mythology theme, and the characters, and I never was bored during any of the books. They are all short reads, so I recommend you give it a try (though they're so popular that it's likely you already have). <br />I will mention that I did get bored with his heros of olympus series. It continues with Percy, but adds a bit of a twist, and I personally thought that Percy's story should have ended at this series. These books were satisfying and great books to own and read second times if you like them. <br />I don't read too much middle reader anymore (though I am a bit confused, because these are shelved with YA at my local bookstore) but these, among several others, are an exception. They are clever, fun, and great to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13536935194375762442" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117658831" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7446542277729725251">I was really impressed and surprised by this series. I loved learning about myths and folklore in middle school, and these books were really refreshing as I got to remember all the Greek gods I'd heard of and learn about a lot more I'd never come across before. <br/><br/>Rick Riordan was clever to make a character from a broken one-parent home with learning disabilities and make him a demigod. His books appeal to his audience very directly, though I feel there's plenty of cross-over for people of varied a</span>
  <span id="freeText7446542277729725251" style="display:none">I was really impressed and surprised by this series. I loved learning about myths and folklore in middle school, and these books were really refreshing as I got to remember all the Greek gods I'd heard of and learn about a lot more I'd never come across before. <br /><br />Rick Riordan was clever to make a character from a broken one-parent home with learning disabilities and make him a demigod. His books appeal to his audience very directly, though I feel there's plenty of cross-over for people of varied ages to enjoy the story. I'm no expert on the Greek myths, but from what I do know, Riordan stayed very true to the mythological characters. (With the exception of Pan in the fourth book. Totally not the Pan I read about, but I guess that's okay. He's the only one I can pinpoint directly.) I loved how adventurous the stories were and the span that they covered with so many characters and monsters and creatures that were fun to interact with. I really have very little bad things to say about this series. I swallowed them all whole. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2625974887" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2625974887" />
    <a title="Sherry Leclerc" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69940418-sherry-leclerc"><img alt="Sherry Leclerc" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503247150p2/69940418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2625974887?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sherry Leclerc" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sherry Leclerc" href="/user/show/69940418-sherry-leclerc">Sherry Leclerc</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="paperback 9781484756881" href="/book/show/40815945-percy-jackson-and-the-olympians-complete-series-and-percy-jackson-s-gree">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2625974887" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer538169164624765678">Percy Jackson and the Olympians is an entertaining and engaging read.<br/><br/>I ordered the Percy Jackson and the Olympians Complete Series to read with my 10 year old son. It was a very enteraining and engaging read. Most nights, my son was begging me to keep reading while I tried to convince him it was time for bed. Honestly, I often wanted to keep going too, but someone has to be the adult ; ) Riordan apparently does the "hook at the end of a chapter" thing very well.<br/><br/>I minored in Classics in Universit</span>
  <span id="freeText538169164624765678" style="display:none">Percy Jackson and the Olympians is an entertaining and engaging read.<br /><br />I ordered the Percy Jackson and the Olympians Complete Series to read with my 10 year old son. It was a very enteraining and engaging read. Most nights, my son was begging me to keep reading while I tried to convince him it was time for bed. Honestly, I often wanted to keep going too, but someone has to be the adult ; ) Riordan apparently does the "hook at the end of a chapter" thing very well.<br /><br />I minored in Classics in University for a couple of semesters until I switched to another subject I felt would be more immediately "useful" for job hunting after graduation. But needless to say, Greek and Roman mythology have been interests of mine for many years. Riordan takes Greek myths and modernizes them. He writes action-filled books with his vision on what Olympus and those classic, mythical gods, heros, and monsters might look like today if they were real, and how the world could be affected. This series is a great way to spark young people's interest in learning more about mythology.<br /><br />Riordan's use of Percy as the protagonist of the series was a very good choice. Like Harry in the Harry Potter series, Percy starts out thinking that he is just a normal kid to whom weird things happen. In Percy's case, a lot of his problems were attributed to ADHD. I believe this approach makes Percy feel more relatable to young people who might themselves feel like they don't always fit in. The unusual family dynamics of the demi-god heros is another aspect that I'm sure many can relate to on many levels.<br /><br />We finished the last book of the series last night, and my son asked me to read the "sneak peek" of the Heros of Olympus series that was previewed at the end. This was obviously a very good marketing strategy, because then I had to go order that series for us to read together. My son made it clear that he wants to start as soon as we recieve it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="538169164624765678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <td colspan="2">

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_862041'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/862041.Harry_Potter_Series_Box_Set"><img alt="Harry Potter Series Box Set (Harry Potter, #1-7)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1534298934l/862041._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/B1EN5oH7TICZwYluVmMpwS3c/+r5FttJIQTEsR6edGBddYXFzAsC4ScswLjPsiN47qv4eUAuMXblpNvlhncPQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }
